Now, more than a year later, the women are able to afford school fees, extra food items, and other goods to benefit their families and communities. Having a disposable income has given the women more economic power in their society.

5/ Follow these coffee beans all the way from seed to cup, through the eyes of Monique Grimaldi, a Volunteer in rural Panama who works with her community on projects in sustainable agriculture. See the full journey here: https://t.co/NfSocuzKhq https://t.co/pxtHUFQ6bK
4/ The fruits start out green, slowly transition into a yellow and then an orange, and finally arrives at the ideal color of red. The best cherries are harvested as the colors 4th and 3rd from the right. https://t.co/OdOYCS8vTD
3/ After the flowers have all come and gone, the production of fruit begins. Each fruit grows no bigger than a blueberry. It‚Äôs an exciting time to watch the colors change and to begin mentally preparing for the harvest that is to come. https://t.co/hlYn5LPKgZ
2/ After 2 - 3 years of development, the coffee tree is ready to bear fruit. The tree‚Äôs sexual maturity can be visibly seen by the clusters of beautiful white flowers that will appear along its branches. Not only are these flowers pleasing to the eye but their scent is sweet. https://t.co/MShghruVwv

5. They innovate in the kitchen. While corn is a steady staple crop in Guatemala, it lacks certain nutrients required for childhood development and a well-rounded diet. 3. They believe in empowering young people. Guatemala's population trends young. More than half of the population is under the age of 19, so it's no surprise that extension agents and Volunteers aim to bring youth into the fold when working on projects in food security. https://t.co/SF1Q2fGHAn
2. They promote nutrition-sensitive agriculture.
